<div class="brown_comment" id="comment_77572823">
  <div class="xhr_comment_photo">
    	<a href="/user/show/1466146-wayne" alt="Wayne"><img alt="M 25x33" src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_25x33-8a3530ed95c3dbef8bf215b080559b09.png" /></a>
  </div>
  <div class="xhr_comment_body">
    <a href="/user/show/1466146-wayne" style="font-weight:bold">Wayne</a>

      
<span id="freeTextContainer11110964937470940345"><em>Wendy wrote: "As a youngster, I always enjoyed the Wind in the Willows cartoon, so when I discovered as an adult that my mom owned a copy and was will</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11110964937470940345"><em>Wendy wrote: "As a youngster, I always enjoyed the Wind in the Willows cartoon, so when I discovered as an adult that my mom owned a copy and was willing to let me borrow it, I thought it automatically followed ..."</em><br /><br />I often think that our first impression of something, (whatever that something may be, and it's endless), does leave a the deepest ...impression!!!<br />I remember a the psychologist, Lorenz ???...first name or last name???, and I am going back to 1967, told the story of how the baby chicks/ducklings(?) when born followed him around as if HE was their mother, because HE was the very FIRST living creature they sighted.<br />It is the same as reading a primer book or a classic comic of a classic novel. At some stage one will meet the Original. It may be Tolstoy's "War and Peace" or Dicken's "A Christmas Carol". Whatever classic it is for a start, will have less illustrations...or NONE at all !!!<br />But you can be sure it will be SUPERIOR in many other ways.<br />I could also compare it to seeing a film before reading the book. I can recall finding the book disappointing in comparison to the film on two occasions - "The Hours " by Michael Cunningham and "The Quiet American" by Graham Greene.<br />All I can do, Wendy, is to assure you that you are a much more complex mechanism than a chick or a duckling, and so there is every chance that you can reread Kenneth Grahame's book and enjoy descriptions, interior thoughts of characters, style of writing etc which a cartoon may not offer; certainly worth a try.<br />Particularly because this book was such a big departure from his other nostalgic books, (although it is so similar in so many ways), and it took time for it to establish itself. It is a book for adults, for everyone,as its values can be appreciated on so many levels. Like the original audience, you are already a Fan...just give your psyche time to adjust to the same wonderful meal in an other guise!!!!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11110964937470940345">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('22qKLwvTvmiN6AAsOpcEbUiY/aUypu+KczhcnC/p/W2+vrX8+QGqkgEwdJdE9uLfAW8+vHt7qCAZMVkO43wLKA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xeBkdfBar3GoC/8RBLomM46LN8PAJPZiVKaG2rKNfhagNFumAoi7iyTTi6p628CBx3z02on5scg+r4NIfhiIUw==')})
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3843.Kenneth_Grahame">About Kenneth Grahame</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3843.Kenneth_Grahame"><img alt="3843" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1201018750p2/3843.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer4303238598482721495">Kenneth Grahame was a British writer, most famous for The Wind in the Willows (1908), one of the classics of children's literature. He also wrote The Reluctant Dragon; both books were later adapted into Disney films.</span>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/3843.Kenneth_Grahame" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Kenneth Grahame...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
